as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/suppdata/apj436934t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-637X/755/2/173\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/suppdata/apj436934t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><h3 id=\"apj436934s2-1\" name=\"apj436934s2-1\">2.1.\u00a0Images at Other Wavelengths</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Follow-up imaging observations of WISE\u00a01814+3412 have been carried out from optical to radio wavelengths, with results summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t1\">1</a>. Details of these observations follow.</p><h4 id=\"apj436934s2-1-1\" name=\"apj436934s2-1-1\">2.1.1.\u00a0Optical Imaging</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Optical imaging of WISE\u00a01814+3412 using <em>g</em>' and <em>r</em>' filters was obtained on UT 2011 May 28 with the Mosaic-1.1 Imager (Sawyer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r70\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r70\">2010</a>) on the KPNO 3.8\u00a0m diameter<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apj436934fn2\">13</a></sup> Mayall telescope. The pixel size was 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />26 at the center of the CCD mosaic, declining to 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />245 at the edge of the 36' field. Three dithered 500\u00a0s exposures in the two filters were obtained in clear conditions with subarcsecond seeing. Pipeline-processed stacked images resampled onto uniform 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />25 pixels were retrieved from the NOAO Science Archive, yielding an FWHM image size of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />75 in <em>g</em>' and 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />70 in <em>r</em>'. Small (~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2) astrometric offsets were made to the image world coordinate system (WCS) to remove any differences with 2MASS catalog positions of objects in the field. Because the WISE\u00a01814+3412 field is not included in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS), flux calibration was obtained using several short (30\u00a0s) observations in the two filters of another W12drop with SDSS coverage 10\u00b0 away. These were immediately followed by 30\u00a0s exposures of WISE\u00a01814+3412 in <em>g</em>', then by full depth 500\u00a0s exposures of WISE\u00a01814+3412 in <em>r</em>', and finally by full depth 500\u00a0s exposures of WISE\u00a01814+3412 in <em>g</em>'. All observations of the two W12drop fields were at an airmass of 1.04 or less. No significant change in zero point was detected between the 30\u00a0s and 500\u00a0s <em>g</em>' exposures on WISE\u00a01814+3412.</p><p>The lower left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f2\">2</a> shows a 2' <b>&#x00d7;</b> 2' region of the reduced <em>r</em>' image centered on WISE\u00a01814+3412, and the upper left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a> shows a zoomed in view of the <em>g</em>' image covering 20'' <b>&#x00d7;</b> 20''. Several objects are apparent near the WISE\u00a01814+3412 coordinates, with the closest being a somewhat extended source (labeled \"A\" in the upper left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a>), two unresolved sources (\"B\" and \"C\") to the north, a fainter source (\"D\") a few arcseconds to the southwest, and two other faint sources farther to the southwest and east. These sources are also seen in the <em>r</em>' image. Components A, B, C, and D were also seen in optical images obtained on UT 2010 June 14 at Palomar Observatory using the Hale 5.08\u00a0m telescope with the Large Format Camera (Simcoe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r75\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r75\">2000</a>) at prime focus. The Palomar images were used to position spectroscopic slits as described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj436934s2-2\">2.2</a>, but because of their relatively poor image quality and nonphotometric conditions these are not further discussed here.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj436934f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj436934f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/755/2/173/Full/apj436934f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/755/2/173/Full/apj436934f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Images of the region near WISE\u00a01814+3412 in <em>g</em>' (0.48\u2009\u03bcm\u2014top left), <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> (2.15\u2009\u03bcm\u2014top right), 4.5\u2009\u03bcm\u2014bottom left, W3 (12\u2009\u03bcm\u2014bottom center), and 350\u2009\u03bcm (bottom right). The field is 20'' on a side with north up and east left. Component\u00a0A is resolved in the <em>g</em>' and <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> images, while B and C are unresolved. Components\u00a0A and D show a Lyman break galaxy spectrum at <em>z</em> = 2.45, component\u00a0C is a broad-lined quasar at <em>z</em> = 2.45, and component\u00a0B is an M-dwarf star. The relative position in the <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> image of component\u00a0A with respect to component\u00a0C is marked with red cross-hairs, showing that component\u00a0A is displaced ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 east in the <em>g</em>' image. Contours at 12 and 350\u2009\u03bcm are from 30% to 90% of the peak in each image. The emission at 12 and 350\u2009\u03bcm is dominated by and centered on component\u00a0A to within the astrometric errors, implying that the other <em>z</em> = 2.45 components (C and D, whose locations are marked with circles) make little contribution to the bolometric luminosity.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj436934f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/downloadFigure/figure/apj436934f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj436934f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj436934f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>Because of the close proximity of source B to A and the fact that source A is extended, the optical photometry for source A reported in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t1\">1</a> is from a 7<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 diameter aperture in an image in which sources B and C have been PSF subtracted. The optical photometry for source B in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t1\">1</a> is from PSF fitting.</p></div><h4 id=\"apj436934s2-1-2\" name=\"apj436934s2-1-2\">2.1.2.\u00a0Near-IR Imaging</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>WISE\u00a01814+3412 was targeted for follow-up in <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> with the NIRC2 camera on the Keck II telescope using laser guide star adaptive optics (Wizinowich et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r80\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r80\">2006</a>) on UT 2010 July 1, and in <em>J</em> on UT 2011 July 20. A total of 30\u00a0minutes of integration were obtained in <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> using dithered 1\u00a0minute exposures, and 18\u00a0minutes in <em>J</em> using 2\u00a0minute exposures, with a pixel scale of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />0397 giving a 40'' field. The <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> data were obtained under photometric conditions and 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />35 seeing, while for <em>J</em> the seeing was &gt;1'' and the sky was cloudy at the end of the night. An <em>R</em> = 15.5 star 33'' from WISE\u00a01814+3412 was used to provide tip-tilt correction.</p><p>Each individual image was sky subtracted using a median of the four preceding and four following images. The sky-subtracted images were roughly registered using the recorded position of the AO tip-tilt sensor stage, and then fine tuned by minimizing their residuals relative to the first image. The final mosaic was formed from the median of aligned images. Photometric calibration was achieved using several well-exposed stars in common with the wider field Palomar/WIRC data described below, but because these exhibited an rms dispersion of 0.2\u00a0mag, that dispersion was imposed as a minimum photometric error. Astrometric calibration was achieved using sources in common with the optical <em>r</em>' image which had been registered to the 2MASS frame (Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj436934s2-1-1\">2.1.1</a>). The upper right panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a> shows the central 20'' <b>&#x00d7;</b> 20'' of the resulting <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> image. Components A, B, C, and D are detected in <em>K<sub>s</sub></em>, while in <em>J</em>, component A is faint and D is undetected. In both images component A is clearly extended relative to components B and C. Photometry was measured in a 50\u00a0pixel (1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />99) diameter aperture for component A and a 20\u00a0pixel (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />79) diameter aperture for component B, centered on the peak of each component.</p><p>A <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> image covering 8<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />7 on the WISE\u00a01814+3412 field was obtained on UT 2010 July 27 and in <em>J</em> on 2011 September 17 with the Wide-field Infrared Camera (WIRC; Wilson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r79\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r79\">2003</a>) at Palomar Observatory using the Hale 5.08\u00a0m telescope. For both images the seeing was subarcsecond and the pixel size was 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />25. The total integration time was 18\u00a0minutes for <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> and 5\u00a0minutes for <em>J</em>, with 1\u00a0minute per dither. The data were flat fielded and coregistered, and calibrated to 2MASS. Although WISE\u00a01814+3412 was only faintly detected in <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> and not at all in <em>J</em> in these data, the WIRC images enabled the photometric calibration of the deeper NIRC2 images to be tied to 2MASS.</p></div><h4 id=\"apj436934s2-1-3\" name=\"apj436934s2-1-3\">2.1.3.\u00a0Spitzer</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>WISE\u00a01814+3412 was observed by <em>Spitzer</em> at [3.6] and [4.5] on 2010 July 22 using Director's Discretionary Time (Program 549). The source was observed with the 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2 pixels and 5' field of each IRAC band using 12 exposures, each 100\u00a0s long, employing the medium scale Reuleaux dither pattern. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f2\">2</a> shows the <em>Spitzer</em> pipeline post-BCD processed image of WISE\u00a01814+3412 at 3.6\u2009\u03bcm, which is resampled onto 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />6 pixels, while Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a> shows the 4.5\u2009\u03bcm image.</p><p>The multiple components seen in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a> are present in the <em>Spitzer</em> data, with the relative prominence of component A increasing at longer wavelengths. Similar to the optical imaging (Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj436934s2-1-1\">2.1.1</a>), the <em>Spitzer</em> photometry for source A reported in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t1\">1</a> is from a 12'' diameter aperture in an image in which sources B and C were PSF subtracted, while the photometry for source B is from PSF fitting. The [4.5] detection is consistent with the <em>WISE</em> W2 given above, while the [3.6] detection implies that the W1 2\u03c3 limit underestimates the true flux density. A minimum photometric error of 0.1\u00a0mag has been imposed on the <em>Spitzer</em> photometry.</p></div><h4 id=\"apj436934s2-1-4\" name=\"apj436934s2-1-4\">2.1.4.\u00a0Far-infrared Data</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>WISE\u00a01814+3412 is undetected by <em>IRAS</em>. Using SCANPI,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apj436934fn3\">14</a></sup> the 2\u03c3 upper limits are &lt;40\u00a0mJy at 12 and 25\u2009\u03bcm, &lt;100\u00a0mJy at 60\u2009\u03bcm, and &lt;600\u00a0mJy at 100\u2009\u03bcm. These limits are consistent with the W3 and W4 detections of WISE\u00a01814+3412.</p></div><h4 id=\"apj436934s2-1-5\" name=\"apj436934s2-1-5\">2.1.5.\u00a0Caltech Submillimeter Observatory Data</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Continuum observations of WISE\u00a01814+3412 at 350\u2009\u03bcm were obtained on 2010 July 13 and 23, and at 450\u2009\u03bcm on 2010 September 12 and 13, using the Submillimeter High Angular Resolution Camera II (SHARC-II) at the 10.4\u00a0m telescope of the Caltech Submillimeter Observatory (CSO) at Mauna Kea, HI (Dowell et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r22\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r22\">2003</a>). SHARC-II uses a bolometer array with 32 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 12 pixels, resulting in a 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />59 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />97 field of view (FOV). The beam sizes of SHARC-II at 350 and 450\u2009\u03bcm are 8<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 and 10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />9, respectively.</p><p>Atmospheric transmission at 350\u2009\u03bcm and 450\u2009\u03bcm is poor when the opacity at 225\u00a0GHz (\u03c4<sub>225</sub>) is &gt;0.07. WISE\u00a01814+3412 was observed near transit for 160\u00a0minutes at 350\u2009\u03bcm with \u03c4<sub>225</sub> = 0.035\u20130.06 and for 90\u00a0minutes at 450\u2009\u03bcm with \u03c4<sub>225</sub> = 0.045. The telescope was scanned in a Lissajous pattern that keeps the source within the FOV. The Dish Surface Optimization System (Leong et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r50\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r50\">2006</a>) was used to correct the dish surface figure for imperfections and gravitational deformations as the dish moves in elevation during observations.</p><p>The SHARC-II data were reduced using version 2.01-4 of the Comprehensive Reduction Utility for SHARC-II (Kov\u00e1cs <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r47\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r47\">2006</a>). Pointing was checked every 1\u20132 hr and corrected to &lt;2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />0 in altitude and &lt;2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 in azimuth using Uranus when available, and with a secondary calibrator, K3-50 (a massive star-forming region close to WISE\u00a01814+3412). The processed 350\u2009\u03bcm image is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f2\">2</a>. Flux calibration was obtained using Uranus. We derive a flux density at 350\u2009\u03bcm of 33 \u00b1 9\u00a0mJy for WISE\u00a01814+3412. At 450\u2009\u03bcm the detection was not significant, with a flux density of 15 \u00b1 10\u00a0mJy. We report in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t1\">1</a> a 95% confidence upper limit of 35\u00a0mJy at 450\u2009\u03bcm, based on the statistical methods described by Feldman &amp; Cousins (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r24\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r24\">1998</a>).</p><p>WISE\u00a01814+3412 was observed at 1.1\u00a0mm with the CSO using the Bolocam instrument for a total of 10 hr on UT 2010 June 18 and 19. Bolocam is a large format camera with 144 detectors, an 8' FOV, and a 30'' FWHM (Haig et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r31\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r31\">2004</a>). The telescope was scanned in a Lissajous pattern keeping the source in the FOV. Pointing was checked and corrected to 6'' using frequent observations of the nearby bright objects K3-50 and 3C345 following methods described in Sayers et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r72\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r72\">2009</a>). Flux calibration, estimated to be accurate to <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 10% (Sandell <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r68\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r68\">1994</a>), was determined using K3-50. Atmospheric contributions to the signal were subtracted using a modified version of the algorithms described in Sayers et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r71\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r71\">2011</a>; see details in Wu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r82\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r82\">2012</a>). The atmospheric subtraction also attenuates astronomical signal, and to account for this, K3-50 was processed in an identical way prior to determining the flux calibration.</p><p>The 1.1\u00a0mm flux density at the location of WISE\u00a01814+3412 is formally \u22120.8\u00a0mJy. The noise fluctuations in the map are Gaussian within our ability to measure them. Including the estimated confusion noise rms per beam of 0.6\u00a0mJy, the estimated total rms per beam at the location of WISE\u00a01814+3412 is 1.6\u00a0mJy. Based on the statistical methods of Feldman &amp; Cousins (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r24\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r24\">1998</a>), the corresponding 95% confidence upper limit is 2.4\u00a0mJy at 1.1\u00a0mm, as listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t1\">1</a>.</p></div><h4 id=\"apj436934s2-1-6\" name=\"apj436934s2-1-6\">2.1.6.\u00a0Radio</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>WISE\u00a01814+3412 was observed with 22 antennas of the D configuration of the Expanded Very Large Array (EVLA) on 2010 June 10. Observations were made simultaneously in two 128\u00a0MHz bands centered on 4.494\u00a0GHz (6.77\u00a0cm, \"<em>C</em>-band low\") and 7.93\u00a0GHz (3.78\u00a0cm, \"<em>C</em>-band high\") in order to obtain a spectral index. The on-source integration time was 29\u00a0minutes. The source J1759+2343 was used for phase calibration and 3C48 was used for flux calibration. The <em>C</em>-band data were calibrated and imaged using Common Astronomy Software Applications<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apj436934fn4\">15</a></sup> (CASA). The 4.494\u00a0GHz image has 39\u2009\u03bcJy/beam rms noise in the 15<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 12<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />3 beam (with major-axis P.A. = \u221242\u00b0), and the 7.93\u00a0GHz image has 67\u2009\u03bcJy/beam noise with an 8<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />7 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 7<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1 beam at P.A. = \u221237\u00b0.</p><p>Source positions and flux densities were estimated from Gaussian fits made by the AIPS task IMFIT. An unresolved source coincident with WISE\u00a01814+3412 to within the astrometric errors (i.e., \u00b10.03 s in R.A. and \u00b10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 in decl.) and a flux density of 560 \u00b1 70\u2009\u03bcJy was detected at 4.494\u00a0GHz (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f2\">2</a>). At 7.93\u00a0GHz, WISE\u00a01814+3412 has a flux density of 350\u2009 \u00b1 \u2009130\u2009\u03bcJy, giving a spectral index \u03b1 \u2248 0.8, where <em>F</em><sub>\u03bd</sub>\u221d\u03bd<sup>\u2212\u03b1</sup>. A second unresolved source was detected 4'' east and 39'' south of WISE\u00a01814+3412 with flux densities of 790 \u00b1 70\u2009\u03bcJy at 4.494\u00a0GHz and 460 \u00b1 120\u2009\u03bcJy at 7.93\u00a0GHz (\u03b1 ~ 1.0). The counterpart to this second source at <em>r</em>' and [3.6] is indicated in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f2\">2</a> with an arrow. Using the spectral indices to extrapolate the EVLA flux densities for the two sources to 1.4\u00a0GHz predicts 1.4\u00a0mJy for WISE\u00a01814+3412 and 2.4\u00a0mJy for the southern source. The sum of these flux densities is consistent with the NRAO VLA Sky Survey (NVSS; Condon et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r17\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r17\">1998</a>) measurement of 3.4 \u00b1 0.5\u00a0mJy, which is a blend of the two sources.</p><p>Observations of WISE\u00a01814+3412 in the Ka band (26\u201340\u00a0GHz, or 9.7\u00a0mm at 32\u00a0GHz) were acquired with the Green Bank Telescope (GBT) on 2010 November 10 using the Caltech Continuum Backend (CCB). A total on-source integration time of 25\u00a0minutes was obtained from 38 useful 1\u00a0minute \"nod\" (beam-switched) observations. The telescope pointing was corrected dynamically with reference to the bright nearby source 1814+4113. The flux calibration was established by an observation of 3C48, which was assumed to have a flux density at 32.0\u00a0GHz of 0.82\u00a0Jy, and a spectral index of \u03b1 = 1.18. This flux density is based on the 32\u00a0GHz brightness temperature measurement of Jupiter (<em>T<sub>J</sub></em> = 146.6 \u00b1 0.75\u2009K; Hill et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r34\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r34\">2009</a>). The data were reduced in publicly available IDL routines custom written to process GBT+CCB data, using the approach described in Mason et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r55\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r55\">2009</a>). All four 3.5\u00a0GHz channels over the 26\u201340\u00a0GHz frequency band were averaged together to maximize the sensitivity, giving a 2\u03c3 upper limit of 175\u2009\u03bcJy for WISE\u00a01814+3412.</p></div></div><h3 id=\"apj436934s2-2\" name=\"apj436934s2-2\">2.2.\u00a0Optical Spectroscopy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We obtained the discovery spectrum revealing that WISE\u00a01814+3412 was at <em>z</em> = 2.452 on UT 2010 May 12 with the dual-beam Low Resolution Imaging Spectrometer (LRIS; Oke et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r61\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r61\">1995</a>) with its Atmospheric Dispersion Compensator (ADC) on the Keck I telescope. Two dithered 600\u00a0s exposures were obtained in clear conditions with subarcsecond seeing. The observations used the 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 wide longslit, the 6800\u2009\u00c5 dichroic, the 400 \u2113\u2009mm<sup>\u22121</sup> grating on the red arm of the spectrograph (blazed at 8500\u2009\u00c5; resolving power <em>R</em> \u2261 \u03bb/\u0394\u03bb ~ 700 for objects filling the slit), and the 400 \u2113\u2009mm<sup>\u22121</sup> grism on the blue arm of the spectrograph (blazed at 3400\u2009\u00c5; <em>R</em> ~ 600). An offset star 22<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1 to the northwest was used to position the spectrograph slit on the <em>WISE</em> source, with a slit position angle (P.A.) of 143<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />6 so that the offset star remained in the slit.</p><p>Additional LRIS-ADC spectroscopy of WISE\u00a01814+3412 and sources in its vicinity (Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj436934s2-1-1\">2.1.1</a>, Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a>) was obtained during UT 2010 July 13\u201315. These observations used the 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 wide longslit, the 5600\u2009\u00c5 dichroic, the 600 \u2113\u2009mm<sup>\u22121</sup> blue grism (blazed at 4000\u2009\u00c5; <em>R</em> ~ 1000), and the same 400 \u2113\u2009mm<sup>\u22121</sup> red grating as used in 2010 May. The nights were photometric. On UT 2010 July 14 two dithered 600\u00a0s exposures were obtained at a P.A. of 8<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />0 to simultaneously observe components A and B, and two dithered 600\u00a0s exposures were obtained at a P.A. of 12<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />0 to simultaneously observe components C and D. On UT 2010 July 15 two dithered 900\u00a0s exposures were obtained at a P.A. of 205<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />0 to simultaneously observe components B and D. In each case, the red arm exposure time was 60\u00a0s shorter than the 600\u00a0s or 900\u00a0s blue arm exposure time. The data were processed using standard procedures and flux calibrated using observations of standard stars from Massey &amp; Gronwall (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r56\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r56\">1990</a>). The reduced spectra are presented in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f4\">4</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj436934f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj436934f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/755/2/173/Full/apj436934f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/755/2/173/Full/apj436934f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Keck/LRIS spectra of optical components near WISE\u00a01814+3412, as marked in the upper left panel of Figure <a href=\"#apj436934f3\">3</a>. Upper left: component A, shifted to the rest frame for <em>z</em> = 2.452. The composite rest-frame ultraviolet spectrum of <em>z</em> ~ 3 LBGs from Shapley et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r74\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r74\">2003</a>) is shown directly below for comparison. Upper right: component B spectrum in the observed frame. This is an optically red point source with spectrum and photometry consistent with an M-dwarf star. Lower left: component C in the rest frame for <em>z</em> = 2.452, showing a bright quasar with narrow self-absorption at the same redshift as WISE\u00a01814+3412. Lower right: component\u00a0D in the rest frame for <em>z</em> = 2.452. The broad Ly\u03b1 absorption, continuum break, and detection of several interstellar absorption lines imply that component\u00a0D is at the same redshift as WISE\u00a01814+3412. The Shapley et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r74\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r74\">2003</a>) composite LBG spectrum is again shown directly below for comparison.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj436934f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/downloadFigure/figure/apj436934f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj436934f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj436934f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The upper left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f4\">4</a> shows the 2010 July spectrum of component A, which is of slightly higher quality than the 2010 May data. WISE\u00a01814+3412 shows a typical Lyman break galaxy (LBG) spectrum at redshift <em>z</em> = 2.452, with Ly\u03b1 emission, a continuum break across the emission line due to the Ly\u03b1 forest, and several UV interstellar absorption lines. The spectrum shows no signs of high ionization, high equivalent width emission lines typical of active galactic nucleus (AGN) activity. For comparison, the LBG composite spectrum from Shapley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r74\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r74\">2003</a>) is shown directly below the component A spectrum in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f4\">4</a>. The 2010 May spectrum shows Ly\u03b1 emission extending &gt;30 kpc to the southeast (P.A. 143<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />6) of component A, making it a Ly\u03b1 blob (Bridge et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r10\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r10\">2012</a>).</p><p>The upper right panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f4\">4</a> shows the combined spectrum from the two P.A.s covering component B, which has a much redder optical spectrum than the other components, and appears to be an early-type M dwarf star. The colors <em>g</em>' \u2212 <em>r</em>' = 1.48, <em>J</em> \u2212 [4.5] = 0.95, <em>K<sub>s</sub></em> \u2212 [3.6] = 0.11, and [3.6] \u2212 [4.5] = 0.17 support this interpretation (Bochanski et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r7\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r7\">2007</a>; Patten et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj436934r62\" id=\"fnref-apj436934r62\">2006</a>).</p><p>The lower left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f4\">4</a> shows the spectrum of component C. This source is a typical broad-lined (i.e., unobscured or Type 1) quasar at the same redshift as WISE\u00a01814+3412. Self-absorption is clearly evident in the Ly\u03b1, Si\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, and C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> transitions.</p><p>The lower right panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj436934f4\">4</a> shows the spectrum of component D. The spectrum has a relatively flat (in <em>F</em><sub>\u03bd</sub>) continuum, with a broad absorption and continuum break at approximately the same wavelength as Ly\u03b1 at <em>z</em> ~ 2.45. Several interstellar absorption lines are evident that match this interpretation, implying that component D is at the same redshift as WISE\u00a01814+3412.</p></div><h3 id=\"apj436934s2-3\" name=\"apj436934s2-3\">2.3.\u00a0Astrometry</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj436934t2\">2</a> gives the measured positions for WISE\u00a01814+3412 components A, B, C, and D when the different components are detected. Only the seconds of right ascension and arcseconds of declination of the coordinates for components B, C, and D are listed. For the <em>WISE</em>, CSO, and radio data, only a single component is detected. A minimum uncertainty of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2 is assumed to account for systematic uncertainties with respect to an absolute reference frame, which is larger than the internal measurement errors for the optical, near-IR, and <em>Spitzer</em> data.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apj436934t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 2.</b>\u00a0Astrometry for WISE\u00a01814+3412</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj436934t2\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/755/2/173/suppdata/apj436934t2_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 2\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\"><th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Band</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">R.A.
